5.11     Tariffs.  The forecasts assume sufficient tariff levels to ensure an
adequate level of net internal cash generation, that tariff increases would be
gradual and that any change in domestic oil prices would be immediately
reflected in the tariffs. Under PERLL Government undertook to cause ONE to
increase its average tariff by 5S on May 1, 1988 (para. 7.02). Under the
proposed project, agreement was reached that an automatic mechanism designed
to protect ONE from fluctuations in its fuel costs attributable to the changes
in hydroelectricity generation will be included in ONE's contract-program and
implemented commencing in 1989 (para. 7.01). The tariff study to be
undertaken (para. 7.02) will include a review of automatic mechanisms used in
other countries to adjust the electricity tariffs to the changes in fuel
prices and to compensate the producers for changes in hydroelectricity
generation. Tariff increases are assumed to take place on May 1 of each
year. They would amount to 52 in 1988, 4% in 1989, 102 in 1990 and 9S in 1991.
5.12     Government Contributions.  Through 1987, Government contributions
financed about 25% of ONE's general investment program, i.e., excluding
investments financed by customers contributions or special projects carried
out on behalf of and funded by the Government (rural electrification and-the
Sahara program in their entirety). The forecasts show that the financing of
ONE's investments up to 1994 without Government capital contributions to its
general program is adequately ensured without impairing its financial
position. Accordingly, under PERL, Government undertook to eliminate its
contributions to ONE's general investment program for the year 1988 (Annex 1).



- 32 -
5.13     Investment Financing.  The sources of finance for ONE's investment
program include: net internal cash generation, Government contributions for
rural electrification and projects in the Sahara Provinces, the proposed Bank
loan, foreign loans and suppliers credits in amounts determined by the
structure of its investment program, and bonds issued on the local market.
5.14     Net Internal Cash Generation.  Because of the inherent difficulties
in performing an adequate assets revaluation and the lumpiness of ONE's
investment program from 1989 onwards, a cash generation covenant, as used in
the two preceding loans to ONE, would be appropriate for monitoring its
financial situation. ONE should achieve a net internal cash generation level
adequate to finance a share of its investment program compatible with its
borrowing ability. This will be particularly important during 1989-1991, when
investments will increase sharply, its tax credit carry-over will end, and the
full adverse impact of debt rescheduling (para. 5.05) will be felt. During
negotiations, ONE agreed to take all necessary measures to achieve, beginning
with fiscal year 1989, a ratio of net internal cash generation to capital
expenditures related to electricity operations, excluding customers'
contributions (other than overhead surcharges) and Government contributions
related to the NREP or to expenditures in selected less developed regions of
at least 25X, on a moving three-year average basis. This figure would
increase to 302 beginning with fiscal year 1991 (para. 7.01). ONE also agreed
to: (i) review at least two months before the end of each fiscal year the
adequacy of ONE's revenues to achieve the agreed net internal cash generation
ratio for that year and the following year and furnish to the Bank the results
of the review; and (ii) on the basis of the above review, take the measures
required to achieve the agreed ratio (para. 7.01). Based on the' above, the
forecasts indicate that tariff increases of about 41 in 1989, 112 in 1990 and
91 in 1991 would be needed to achieve the above objectives over the period
1989 - 1994. Its carry-over tax credit being exhausted, ONE would start
paying income tax in 1989 and would be fully subject to it from 1990 on at a
452 rate. From 1987 to 1994, the total transfers from ONE to Government
(income tax, import taxes, and other indirect taxes, including VAT but
excluding the large indirect tax on crude oil which raises the domestic price
for heavy fuel oil used by ONE to about double the international price (para.
1.19) would amount to DH 10,403 million. As shown in Table 5.4, ONE would
move from being a small net contributor to Government in 1986 to being a very
large net contributor from 1989 onwards.
5.15     Debt Limitation - ONE's financial performance should be such as to
allow ONE to service its debt adequately without impairing its self-financing
ability. Agreement was therefore obtained that ONE shall not incur any
long-term debt without Bank approval unless a reasonable forecast of its
projected net revenues for each year during the term of the debt to be
incurred shall be at least 1.5 times the projected debt service requirement in
such year on all debt of ONE (para. 7.01). Borrowing is expected to increase
from about 291 of investment requirements in 1989 to about 682 in 1994. ONE's
debt service coverage ratio would remain above 1.7 and its debt/equity ratio
would remain satisfactory.
5.16     Key indicators of ONE's forecast financial performance during
1987-1994 are summarized in Table 5.4 :

5.17     Accounting.  ONE's financial staff is good.  The Finance Department has
highly competent and dedicated management who have considerably improved the
quality of ONE's accounts and financial analysis techniques. However, because of
better salaries offered elsewhere, a high staff turnover has occurred in recent
years at the intermediate level.
5.18     ONE's accounting system is derived from the 1957 French accounting
system.  Major accounts are computerized and monthly and quarterly statements are
prepared. ONE recently introduced microcomputers in several departments, which
will considerably accelerate the preparation and analysis of accounts. It also
plans to introduce computerized financial forecastiirg and analysis based on a
model used by the Bank.
5.19     Under PERL, the current system of a priori control of commitments and
expenditures by the Financial Comptroller and the Government Accountant (both
representatives of the Ministry of Finance) will be made more flexible with the
introduction of improved procedures for oversight of ONE's financial operations
(para. 7.02). This will require a reporting system based on reliable accounting
and management information, together with appropriate auditing procedures. To
achieve the latter, ONE intends to strengthen its internal control division; its
scope would be expanded and additional qualified staff would be recruited and
trained. These arrangements are satisfactory.
5.20     External Auditing  Under Loan 1695-M0R, ONE agreed to have its financial
statements audited by independent auditors acceptable to the Bank and to send a
copy of the audit report to the Bank not later than seven months after the end of
the fiscal year. These arrangements have worked well. The current audit
provisions are satisfactory and are repeated under the proposed loan (para. 7.01).
5.21     Insurance.  ONE carries insurance for workman's compensation and third
party liability. However, since it terminated its coverage with commercial
insurers in the early 1970s, ONE's assets have not been insured against risks
such as fire, explosion and natural calamities with private insurance companies.
ONE agreed to take out and maintain with responsible insurers or to make other
provisions satisfactory to the Bank for insurance against such risks. To this
effect, ONE plans to undertake an analysis of the appropriate measures to take
concerning insurance of its assets, including among others the option of setting
up a reserve, and will furnish to the Bank the results of this analysis not later
than December 31, 1988.
B. THE REGIES
5.22     Past Financial Performance  Key indicators describing the recent
financial performance of the five participating Regies are shown in Annexes
15.1-15.18 and summarized below:
Table 5.5
Consolidated Financial Indicators (Five Regies)
1984 - 1986 (in DH Million)
1984      1985        1986
Operating Revenues                            1,246      1,397       1,516
Operating Expenses                            1,244      1,437       1,515
Net Income                                        0       (42)           0
Net Internal Cash Generation                     49         14          63
Consumer Contributions                           83         93          95
Investment Program                              164        182         166



- 35 -
The Regies are financially autonomous enterprises. They buy electricity from
ONE and resell it to consumers at prices approved by Government (Annexes
4.1-4.3).   Average purchasing and selling prices (including taxes) differ
from R6gie to Regie, and range from DR 0.64 to DH 0.68 for purchases and from
DH 0.78 to DH 0.81 for sales, for the five participating Regies on May 1, 1987.
5.23     Each tariff increase granted to ONE induces a tariff increase for the
Regies. However, anxious to keep the price of electricity sold to a minimum,
the Government did not permit increases in the Regies' price margins for
several years prior to 1986. Since the Regies' operating expenses increased
because of inflation and system expansion, operating income has in general
declined in recent years and, in some cases, became negative in 1986. Twe
notable exceptions are the Rabat and Tanger Regies, where the average margins
have remained sufficiently high so as not to affect their financial
situation. Another complication is that the introduction in May 1984 of a
progressive tariff for low voltage consumers affected the various Regies
differently, because of the varying composition of consumers among blocks. As
a result, some Regies experienced a reduction in their average margins. In
May 1987, and for all R6gies, the average margin and average sales price for
kWh were larger for medium-voltage than for low-voltage customers; the low-
voltage margin for the first block was negative for the Casablanca Regie.
5.24     The Regies finance investments through net internal cash generation,
customers' contributions and, to a minimal extent, long-term debt. Customers
contributions are made up of three components: (i) the cost of a new
connection, excluding overhead; (ii) 20% of the cost of the connection, to
cover overhead; and (iii) a one-time contribution towards network expansion.
These contributions vary considerably from year to year. They typically
represent more than 50X of annual investment requirements and have a major
impact on the Regies' financial situation. However, no systematic attempt has
been made up to now to forecast contributions with some degree of accuracy.
The Regies should develop a system which would allow better financial
forecasts of these contributions by splitting their investment programs into
homogeneous slices, corresponding to identifiable construction projects, and
separately analyzing the timing and amount of the related contributions.
During negotiations, each of the five participating Regies agreed to undertake
a study, on terms of reference agreed with the Bank, analyzing the assessment
of their consumers contributions in relation with the corresponding works in
participation, in order to uniformize the methods used to assess them and to
inform systematic projections (para. 7.01). This study should be completed by
September 30, 1988 and its recommendations should be implemented before July
31, 1989. In addition the Government plans to make all efforts so that the
non-participating Regies will carry out the same study.
5.25     Accounte Receivable  Collection from domestic and industrial
customers is generally adequate because the R6gies immediately disconnect the
service in case of overdue payments. In contrast, Government arrears have
accumulated over the years. At the end of 1985, Government arrears for energy
and related works amounted for the five Regies (except Kenitra) to DH 284
million (eight months of billing in Casablanca). However, as a result of the
new procedures enacted by the Government in May 1984 (para. 5.09), the Regies
reported that the current receivables situation from the Government
departments has somewhat improved. In order to complement the commitments
made under PERL on the settlement of arrears from Government, it was agreed
during negotiations that (a) each of the Government's administrative
subdivisions shall pay its electricity bills to all the Regies promptly in



- 36 -
accordance with guidelines satisfactory to the Bank (para. 7.01). For this
purpose, the guidelines in the May 1984 Government circular would be
satisfactoty. It was also agreed that (b) each of the Government's
administrative subdivisions shall pay to all the Regies their arrears for
electricity and works as of July 31, 1988 in equal yearly installments
commencing not later than September 30, 1988, with the last payment to be made
not later than September 30, 1992 (para. 7.01). In addition, (c) the five
participating R6gies will pay their bills to ONE not later than the earlier of
their due date or sixty days after the date of the bill; and (d) the balance
of the arrears for energy owed by the five participating Regies to ONE after
the general compensation of arrears within the public sector implemented under
PERL will be paid in equal yearly installments commencing on September 30,
1988 with the last payment not later than September 30, 1992 (para. 7.01).
The Government plans to make all efforts so that the non-participating Regies
abide by the provisions of (c) and (d).
5.26     Investment Financing.  As a result of the Government's policy to
reserve access to Morocco's small domestic capital market to ONE, the
electricity departments of the Regies have incurred only minimal debt. Water
sector investments of the Regies are considered higher priority and water
tariffs before 1987 were inadequate to contribute to the financing of water
sector investments. Therefore, most Regies have been financing part of the
water sector construction program through transfers from their electricity
departments without interest. This form of financing has increased
considerably during recent years (in Casablanca for instance, from an
accumulated DH 135 million in 1983 to DH 297 million in 1986).  Thus, faced
with dwindling cash generation, an increase in Government arrears, the need to
finance part of the construction program of their water departments and their
inability to borrow, the Regies' electricity departments had to postpone some
of their investments. In additions they frequently had to delay payments to
their suppliers, notably ONE. The Regies' arrears to ONE increased
considerably in recent years (for instance, from DI 127 million in 1983 to
about DR 521 million in 1986 in Casablanca, or 7.0 months of electricity
purchases).
5.27     Future Financial Performance.  Key indicators of the five
participating R6gies are given in Table 5.6.
5.28     Policy adjustments are needed to make the electricity departments of
the R6gies sound financial entities. Under PERL and the present project, the
existing arrears for energy of government entities and public enterprises will
be settled. Under the proposed loan, it was agreed during negotiations that:
(a) the five participating Regies will take measures starting in fiscal year
1988 so that they will generate total revenues equivalent to at least total
operating expenses related to electricity operations and a ratio of net
internal cash generation to annual capital expenditures (excluding customers'
contributions other than overhead surcharges) of at least 302, based on a
moving three-year average and (b) financing of a participating Regie's water
department by its electricity department will be allowed only when payables to
ONE do not exceed two months of purchases (para. 7.01). Each participating
R6gie also agreed to: (i) review, at least two months before the end of each
fiscal year, the adequacy of its revenues to achieve, on the basis of a
realistic forecast, the agreed net internal cash generation ratio for such
year and the following year and furnish a copy of such a review to the Bank;
and (ii) on the basis of the above review, take the measures required to
achieve the agreed ratios (para. 7.01).

5.30     Accounting.  All Regies maintain separate accounts for their
electricity and water departments. Cash and bank accounts are maintained for
the Regie as a whole, but a treasury account in each of the two departments'
balance sheets reflects their respective shares of the joint resources and the
extent to which one department has subsidized the other. General overhead is
allocated 251 to water and 751 to electricity.
5.31     The present accounting system is a version of the 1957 French
accounting system and includes both general and cost accounting. Despite
basic similarities among the systems in use in the different R6gies, each one
has its own distinctive features because of the absence of a standard Manual.
This lack of standardization complicates comparison of financial performance
between Regies. Although the current system has its own rationale, it is
nonetheless based on accounting methods which are more often than not at
variance with generally accepted accounting principles. As a result, the
Regies' official financial statements frequently do not present fairly their
financial situation."' Primary examples of the weaknesses of the present
accounting practices are:
(a) the exclusion, for fiscal reasons, of the "surtaxe de de oppement"
and the 201 surcharge to all new consumers over and above the actual cost
of their connections, from the revenue base; (b) the absence in most
Regies of a depreciation policy based on expected asset lives; and (c) the
absence of an account for work in progress.
1/  The financial statements attached in Annex 15 have been restated in
accordance with Bank requirements and standardized to allow comparisons
between Regies.



- 39 -
5.32     The need to reform the present system is generally accepted.  The
Government has been preparing a new National Accounting System with the
assistance of independent experts financed under PERL. An action plan to
gradually implement this system in both the water and electricity departments
of all R6gies by January 1, 1990 was agreed under the National Water Supply
Rehabilitation Project (para. 7.03) and Government indicated that this system
is planned to be introduced in 1988. It was also agreed under the same
project to engage consultants to examine and redesign the cost accountipg
systems of both the water and electricity departments of the Regies and to
implement a cost accounting system satisfactory to the Bank by January 1, 1989
(para. 7.03).
5.33     The Regies have, up to now, been subject to different income tax
rules. The problem arises mainly for historical reasons and because of
divergent interpretations of the fiscal laws by local tax inspectors. During
negotiations, Government confirmed that, starting with fiscal year 1988, all
the Regies will be subject to the general tax laws of corporations and that
from the tax point ofljview, the electricity, water and sewerage departments of
each Regie will be considered as separate entities.
5.34     Auditing.  The R6gies' accounts are subject to a Rriori government
control through a Government Accountant and a Financial Comptroller and a
posteriori control by the Cour des Comptes. Measures to provide greater
autonomy to the Regies to make procurement decisions are included under the
National Water Supply Rehabilitation Project (Annex 1). It has also been
agreed under this project that all the R6gies' accounts will be audited from
1988 onwards by independent auditors acceptable to the Bank, and their
financial statements and audit reports furnished to the Bank within six months
of each fiscal year. This agreement was reconfirmed under the present project
(para. 7.01).
5.35     Some Regies have an internal audit unit which functions quite well,
especially in the larger entities. In the smaller Regies, the emphasis is
more on routine verification of clerical accuracy. Greater efficiency could
be achieved by developing, or strengthening, internal audit units within the
R6gies. This will require training of internal auditors for those R6gies
where such skills are lacking (para. 5.37).
5.36     Personnel and Training.  Implementation of a new accounting system
,will not cause problems for the larger Regies' top financial officers, who are
well acquainted with commercial accounting systems. Some training in
commercial accounting would, however, be necessary for middle and lower level
accounting staff of all Regies. In addition, training of selected staff in
internal auditing and applied financial computer programming would be required.
5.37     The Inter-Regie Training Center (Centre Inter-R6gies de Formation
Professionelle - CIRFP) was created in 1975. It has been quite effective in
training lower level technical staff from all Regies. The Center, which is
operated by RAD, is jointly owned and financed by all the R6gies and has a
capacity of about 116 students a year. In 1985, following an assessment by
RAD of the Regies' training needs, it was decided to increase CIRFP's
capability to adequately meet the training requirements of accounting and
financial staff. More specifically, CIRFP needs to build its capabilities to:



- 40 -
(i) develop refresher courses to acquaint technical staff with new techniques
and equipment before their introduction; (ii) train accounting and financial
staff in commercial accounting; (iii) introduce staff to microcomputer
programming; and (iv) train internal auditors. Provision was made under the
National Water Supply Rehabilitation Project for consultant services and
technical assistance to RAD to: (i) assess the training needs of the Regies;
(ii) acquire materials and equipment for the training center; and (iii) design
and assist in the implementation of appropriate new training programs. The
proposed Project will make funds available, as a supplement to the provisions
made under the water supply loan, to grant fellowships for selected staff, to
acquire training materials (including microcomputers) and to provide other
training services (para. 4.11).
5.38     Management Information System (MIS)   Data processing and billing are
centrally handled by a data processing corporation--Societe Inter-R6gie de
Traitement Informatique-- (SIRTI) jointly owned by all the Regies. There is,
however, an acute need for the Regies to develop a reliable Management
Information System and to acquire computer equipment. Presently, and in the
absence of such a system, the quality of the data base available to most
R6gies does not allow them to carry out tariff analyses and other important
studies such as the analysis of the structure of consumers' contributions
(para. 5.24). In order to introduce a comprehensive and standardized MIS, and
to satisfy the urgent need for decentralized computer equipment, a study to
carry out an MIS review will be commissioned under the National Water Supply
Rehabilitation project. Under this loan, agreement was reached that the
Regies will implement a suitable Management Information System by September
30, 1989 (para. 7.03). Ftrthermore, and in order to satisfy the Regies'
urgent need for a decent lized computer equipment, funds will be provided
under the proposed Project to acquire some micro and mini computers (para.
4.11).
5.39     Insurance  The Regies carry insurance with Moroccan insurance
companies covering their assets, and also insurance for workman's compensation
and third party liability. The insurance provisions for the Regies are
satisfactory.



- 41 -
VL PROJECT JUSTIFICATION
6.01     Relationship to Policy Obiectives.  The Project forms an essential
part of the Bank's strategy for assistance to Morocco's power subsector as
outlined in Chapter I since it would:
(i)    contribute to expanding electricity supplies in an economically
efficient manner;
(ii)    help ensure that ONE and the R6gies achieve a satisfactory financial
performance and make significant net financial contributions to
Government; and
(iii)   contribute to strengthening the management and planning capability of
the power subsector.
6.02     Least-Cost Justification.  The economic evaluation of distribution
system investments is difficult because of many geographical centers and many
small investments, some for expansion, others for rehabilitation. On the
basis of examinations by Bank staff of the growth in demand for electricity
and for new connections (paras. 3.02 and 3.07) and of the distribution system
investment programs of ONE and the five participating Regies, it is judged
that these programs are appropriate and that the components proposed for Bank
financing are high-priority. Similarly, the expenditures on spare parts,
power station rehabilitation and system improvement proposed for Bank
financing by ONE are judged to be appropriate and high-priority.
6.03     The coordinated investment study to be financed under  PERL (para.
7.02) has as its objictive the preparation of a coordinated least-cost
investment program for the power sub-sector as a whole. The actions outlined
in para. 3.10 are designed to ensure the implementation and regular updating
of the coordinated least-cost programs of ONE and the R6gies. The
distribution planning analyses for ONE (para. 3.06) would further strengthen
ONE's capacity to prepare least-cost investment programs for its distribution
system.
6.04     Economic Rate of Return.  Since the Project forms an integral part of
,the investment programs of ONE and the five participating Regies, the economic
rate of return was calculated on the investments undertaken to supply the
projected incremental sales of electricity over the project implementation
period (1988 through 1994). The assumptions used in the analysis are set out
in Annex 16.
6.05     The measured benefits include: (a) incremental revenues of ONE and
the five R6gies over the period 1988 through 1994; and (b) reductions in
distribution losses and in operating and maintenance costs. Tariff
adjustments were projected in line with those estimated in Chapter V as being
needed to achieve satisfactory self-financing levels for the six entities.



- 42 -
6.06     The measured costs include: (a) capital costs needed to supply the
incremental sales over the period 1988 through 1994; (b) fuel costs of
incremental generation; and (c) other operating and maintenance costs of ONE
and the five Regies associated with the incremental electricity demanded.
Fuel costs were evaluated at international fuel prices assumed to increase
according to a projection made by Bank staff. Import duties and taxes were
excluded, but physical contingencies were included in the investment estimates.
6.07     Under the above assumptions, the calculated rate of return is 12.4%,
which is well above the estimated opportunity cost of capital of 102.
However, it substantially understates the real economic return since it
excludes the consumer's surplus. Annex 16 presents the results of some
sensitivity tests.

V1L AGREEMENTS REACHED AND RECOMMENDATION
7.01     During negotiations agreement was reached on the following actions:
(i) by December 31, 1989, distribution planning analyses for ONE will be
completed on terms of reference and conditions acceptable to the Bank
and by January 1, 1992 measures agreed between the Bank and ONE will
be taken to implement recommendations based on the analyses (para.
3.06);
(ii)    by October 31 of 1988 and each succeeding year, ONE and the five
participating Regies will each consult with the Bank on its updated
investment program for the following five years (para. 3.iO);
(iii)   the Government will maintain a technical committee with membership
and terms of reference satisfactory to the Bank, to be responsible
for facilitating the coordination of ONE and the participating Regies
in the preparation of their respective investment programs (para.
3.10);
(iv)    by October 31 of each year, the technical committee will furnish to
the Bank for review a proposed coordinated investment program for the
power subsector and thereafter take measures to ensure implementation
of the program which the Bank agrees is designed to ensure the proper
development of the subsector (para. 3.10);
(v)   by December 31, 1989, ONE and the five participating Regies, after
taking account of the final report of the coordinated investment
study and after consultation with the Bank, will take actions to
strengthen the demand forecasting and planning capacities of ONE and
the Regies and to facilitate proper coordination among these entities
in forecasting demand and planning new investments (para. 3.10);
(vi)    by June 30, 1988, the five participating Regies will furnish to the
Bank detailed programs for training for R6gie personnel and
acquisition of computer hardware and software by the Regies (para.
4.11);
(vii)   the Government will enter into subsidiary Loan Agreements with ONE
and the five Regies on terms and conditions acceptable to the Bank.
Conclusion of these agreements will constitute a condition of
effectiveness (para. 4.15);
(viii)  the Government will open and maintain in dollars a special account
(Revolving Fund) of US$4 million in its Central Bank on terms and
conditions satisfactory to the Bank (para. 4.21);
(ix)    Government will ensure that amounts due to ONE by its administrative
subdivisions on account of electricity and related works shall be
paid promptly in accordance with guidelines satisfactory to the Bank
(para. 5.09).
(x)    Government will ensure that amounts due to ONE by its administrative
subdivisions and existing at July 31, 1988 for electricity and



- 44 -
related works are paid in equal annual installments beginning on
September 30, 1988 and ending not later tnan September 30, 1992
(para. 5.09).
(xi)    ONE will pay its fuel bills within thirty days after the due dates of
such bill (para. 5.09);
(xii)   an automatic mechanism to compensate ONE for changes in fuel expenses
due to fluctuations in hydroelectricity generation will be included
in ONE's contract-program and implemented in 1989 (para. 5.11);
(xiii)  ONE will take measures to produce, beginning with fiscal year 1989, a
net internal cash generation equivalent to at least 25% of its
consumers' contributions other than overhead surcharges or capital
expenditures (excluding Government contributions related to the NREP
or to investments in selected less developed regions) on a moving
three-year average basis increasing to 302 beginning with fiscal year
1991 (para. 5.14);
(xiv)   ONE and the five participating Regies will: (i) review at least two
months before the end of each fiscal year the adequacy of ONE's and
the five participating R6gies' revenues to achieve the agreed net
internal cash generation ratio for such year and the following year;
and (ii) on the basis of the above review, the measures required to
achieve the agreed ratios (paras. 5.14 and 5.28);
(xv)    ONE shall not incur any long-term debt without Bank approval unless a
reasonable forecast of its projected net revenues for each year
during the term of the debt to be incurred shall be at least 1.5
times the projected debt service requirement in such year on all debt
of ONE (para. 5.15);
(xvi)   ONE's accounts will be audited by independent auditors acceptable to
the Bank and its financial statements and audit reports will be
furnished to the Bank within seven months after the end of each
fiscal year (5.20);
(xvii)  the five participating Regies will undertake a study, on terms of
reference agreed with the Bank, to analyze and coordinate the
assessment of their consumers' contributions in relation to their
works in participation. This study should be completed by September
30, 1988 and its recommendations implemented before July 31, 1989
(para. 5.24);
(xviii) Government will ensure that amounts due to all the Regies by its
administrative subdivisions on account of sales of electricity and
related works are paid promptly in accordance with guidelines
satisfactory to the Bank (para. 5.25);
(xix)   Government will ensure that amounts due to all the Regies by its
administrative subdivisions and existing at July 31, 1988 for
electricity and related works are paid in equal annual installments
beginning on September 30, 1988 and ending not later than September
30, 1992 (para. 5.25);
i

(xx)    the five participating R6gies will ensure that bills payable by them
to ONE are paid not later than the earlier of their due date or 60
days after the date of the bill (para. 5.25);
(xxi)   the balance of the arrears for energy owed by the five participating
Regies to ONE as of July 31, 1988 after the PERL compensation will be
paid by the Regies in equal annual installments commencing on
September 30, 1988 with the last payment not later than September 30,
1992 (para. 5.25);
(xxii)  the five Regies will take measures starting with fiscal year 1988 to
generate a positive net income and a net internal cash generation
equivalent to at least 30% of annual capital expenditures (excluding
customers' contributions other than overhead surcharges) on a moving
three-year average basis (para. 5.28);
(xxiii) financing of a participating R6gie's water department by its
electricity department will be allowed only when payables to ONE do
not exceed two months of electricity purchases (para. 5.28);
(xxiv)  from 1988 onwards, the R6gies' accounts will be audited by
independent auditors acceptable to the Bank and their financial
statements and audit reports will be furnished to the Bank within six
months of the end of each fiscal year (5.34);
7.02     During negotiations agreement was reached to include under the
Project the following commitments made under PERL:
{i)    by September 30, 1988 the Government will develop and furnish to the
Bank proposed policies and procedures for the oversight of ONE's
financial operations, and by January 1, 1989 and after exchanging
views with ONE and the Bank, implement these policies and
procedures. By October 31, 1988 ONE will prepare and furnish to the
Bank for review and comments a three-year corporate development plan
setting forth its development objectives and performance targets and
actions to achieve these objectives and targets, and by November 30,
1988 and after exchanging views with the Government and the Bank,
conclude arrangements with the Government to implement the plan. The
plan will be monitored according to guidelines satisfactory to the
Bank and any revisions will require agreement by the Bank. (The
corporate development plan and the Government's policies and
procedures for financial oversight will be included in a
contract-program for ONE).
(ii)    by May 1, 1988 ONE will increase its tariff rates by an average of 5%
above the rates in effect after the 1987 increase;
(iii)   by March 31, 1989 a study will be completed and furnished to the
Bank, on terms of reference acceptable to the Bank, with the
objectives of determining electricity tariff rates which reflect long
run marginal costs; and by October 31, 1989 the Government will
implement recommendations based on this study as shall have been
agreed between the Government and the Bank.



- 46 -
(iv)    by November 30, 1988 a study will be completed and furnished to the
Bank, on terms of reference acceptable to the Bank, with the
objective of developing a least-cost, coordinated investment program
for the power subsector, and recommendations based on the study will
be implemented after consultation with the Bank;
(v)    by October 31, 1989, ONE will develop and fuAduis.h to the Bank, on
terms of reference acceptable to the Bank, an appropriate management
information system (MIS) and thereafter introduce this system on the
basis of an exchange of views with the Bank;
7.03     During negotiations agreement was reached to include under the
Project the following commitments made under the National Water Supply
Rehabilitation Project: the five participating R6gies will develop, on the
basis of guidelines satisfactory to the Bank, and introduce and apply: (a) not
later than January 1, 1989 a suitable cost accounting system; (b) not later
than September 30, 1989, a suitable management information system; and (c) not
later than January 1, 1990, a suitable general accounting system.
7.04     With the above agreements the proposed Project is suitable for a Bank
loan of $90 million, for a term of 20 years at the standard variable interest
rate, including a five-year grace period, to the Kingdom of Morocco.

MOROCCO
POWER DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
Estimates of the Long-Run Marginal Cost of Electricity
1.       For the purpose of comparing tariff revenue to the economic cost of
electricity supply, estimates were made of long-run marginal costs for ONE and
the largest Regie, Casablanca. These are preliminary calculations intended to
determine only whether the level of marginal costs is significantly greater or
less than average revenue. A definitive analysis of the structure of marginal
costs will be provided by the study of tariffs to be financed by PERL. The
assumptions used to make the estimates are described here.
Capital Cost of Generation
2.       An increment of demand of 1 kW is assumed to be added to the forecast
demand for each year from 1987 on. Prior to 1989 this demand can be met from
existing capacity. In 1989, the incremental demand would require additional
capacity during peak periods. Since ONE plans to bring into service in 1989 a
90 MW combustion turbine designed to run on treated fuel oil, the present
calculations assume that the incremental demand would be met by added
combustion turbine capacity.
3.       A new 90 MW (net) combustion turbine with a capital cost of DH 300
million (end 1985 prices and exchange rate, ONE estimate) would have a present
value in 1989 of DH 3651 per kW in December 1987 prices and exchange rate
assuming a two year construction period and a 102 discount rate. Assuming a
20 year life, and a 202 reserve margin, the equivalent annuity would be DH 515
per kW. For the purpose of calculating the marginal cost in 1987, it is
assumed that the capital cost of the combustion turbine would be amortized
over 21.5 years starting in 1988 rather than in 1989 when the unit enters
service. Spreading the capital cost over the longer period reduces the
annuity to DH 446 per kW.
Energy Costs
4.       The marginal energy cost was calculated by ONE using a load
dispatching optimization model and a price of fuel oil equal to the export
price (estimated at $104 per ton in April 1987). The results were adjusted to
reflect non-fuel operating costs of DH 0.0135 per kWh. Fuel plus operating
costs were estimated by this approach to be DH 0.226 per kWh for 1987.



_ 62 -
ANNEX 5
Page 2 of 5
Transmission Cost
5.       The transmission capacity cost was calculated by the average
incremental cost method using ONE's investment program for the period
1987-1990 (excluding taxes) together with projected demand growth of 7S per
year.  Adding operating costs of DR 82 per kW per year gives a total of DH 346
per kW per year, assuming a 30 year lifetime.
Distribution Cost (ONE)
6.       The distribution capacity cost for ONE was calculated by the average
incremental cost method using ONE's distribution investment program (excluding
taxes and expenditures prefinanced by customers) for the years 1987-1990,
together with projected demand growth of 72 per year. Adding operating costs
of DR 532 per kW per year yields a total of DR 1402 per kW per year, assuming
a 30 year lifetime. A split between low voltage and medium voltage
expenditure was not available.
Distribution Cost (Mtgie of Casablanca)
7.       The distribution capacity cost for Casablanca was calculated by the
average incremental cost method using the Regie's distribution investment
program (excluding taxes and expenditures prefinanced by customers) for the
years 1987-1990, together with projected demand growth averaging 6.71 per
year. Adding operating costs calculated from the Income Statement (Annex
15.3) to be DR 351 per kW per year yields a total of DR 737 per kW per year.
Transmission and Distribution Losses
8.       Transmission losses were 7.01 of net electricity generation in 1985,
and ONE's distribution losses were 8.32 of energy delivered to its
distribution network in 1985. Casablanca's distribution losses were 7.0S of
energy delivered to the R6gie in 1986.
Summary of LonR Run Marginal Costs
9.       The capacity cost estimates were calculated per kWh using ONE's load
factor of 651. They were combined with energy and other operating costs and
losses as follows:

Fuel Price Sensitivity
10.      The marginal cost estimates are sensitive to changes in the price of
heavy fuel oil. When the marginal cost is re-estimated using a fuel oil price
of DR 1770 per ton, the average domestic price paid by ONE in 1987, the
weighted average LRMC for ONE increases to DH 0.70, compared to DH 0.45 when
the international fuel oil price is used.
Shadow Exchange Rate Sensitivity
11.      The marginal cost estimates are also sensitive to assumptions about
the foreign exchange rate. Usinig a shadow rate of exchange, estimated by Bank
staff to be US$1 = DR 10.4 (as compared to the December 1987 rate of US$1 * Dl
8.0), raises the weighted average LRMC for ONE from DH 0.45 per kWh to DR 0.56
per kWh.

ANNEX 13.3
-101-                      Page 1 of 3
MOROCCO
POWER DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
Proiect MonitorLng Guidelines
1.       The monitoring guidelines given below indicate the broad requirements
on records, which the beneficiaries should maintain to monitor the progress of
the Project and permit its evaluation on completion.
General
2.       Records will be maintained giving forecast against actual
achievements, at agreed intervals, for the following:
(a) sales, losses and purchases;
(b)  economic breakdown of sales;
(c) number of consumers;
(d) gross revenue and cost of purchases;
(e) revenue per kWh, and cost of purchase per kWh;
(f) frequency distribution of consumption (sales);
(g) stocks;
(h) personnel;
(i)  bydro data;
(j) power generation; units generated in GWh by station;
(k) installed and derated generation capacity in MW for each of the power
stations and according to type (such as hydro, thermal);
(1) energy and peak demand;
(m) fuel consumption for each of the units in the power stations;
(n) network inventory;
(o) quality of service (forced and planned outages, duration, causes,
etc.);



-102-                        ANNEX 13.3
Page 2 of 3
(p) expenses (maintenance, fuel, other consumables, personnel, other);
(q) revenues (LV, MV, RV and other revenues);
(r) investment program; and
(s) compliance with loan conditions
Note: The items (i) to (m) refer to ONE only.
Prolect Implementation
3.       Records will be maintained, comparing the original schedule against
actual achievements on the following aspects:
(a) problems bearing on the Project and corrective actions taken;
(b) progress (and/or delays) of each main activity under the Project such
as procurement, construction, studies, training, commissioning and
start of operation of plant, operational difficulties, etc.;
(c) information on Physical Progress, accompanied by the explanation for
any reasonably substantial change;
(d)  status of tenders and contract awards, accompanied by explanation of
any reasonably substantial change. Similarly for management of
services;
(e) any expected reasonably substantial change in design, lay-out,
physical execution or procurement action should be reported in
advance, giving adequate justification for the proposed change;
(f) brief individual paragraphs, indicating progress and problems in
administration, accounting, studies, and supervision of the Project;
(g) training, shortcomings of the program and recommended corrective
measures;
(h)  actual Project costs and expenditures (local and foreign) and
estimated remaining expenditures (local and foreign); projected on an
annual basis through Project completion;
(i) disbursement schedule (for Bank loan and any other loans); and
(j) environmental issues connected with the Project.



ANNEX 13.3
-103-                       Page 3 of 3
Financial
4.       At the end of each quarter the financial accounts (income statements,
changes in financial position state_ents and balance sheets) for the period
1987-1994, actual and forecasts, according to the format used in the appraisal
report of the project.
5.       Compliance with loan conditions.
December 1987

ONE
Notes and assumptions on the financial statements
Inflation rates (in 2)
1986    1987   1988   1989   1990   .991   1992   1993   1994
Local              10.0    5.4      7.0    7.0    7.0      7.0    7.0    7.0   7.0
International      12.0   10.9      1.0    1.0    1.0      3.5    3.5    3.5   3.5
Income statement
-   Sales of energv:  Tariff increases are assumed to take place on May
1. Sales include the Value Added Tax (VAT), (7%).
Other operatint revenues: ONE's mark-up on works performed by
customers for themselves, sales of scrap, meters, investment income,
Fuel (excluding VAT):
fuel-oil and gas-oil: constant July 1987 price. Includes a tax
assessed at the refinery level by the Government.
local coal (Casablanca and Jerada, separately): July 1987 price
indexed by local inflation.
imported coal: Price/ton FOB in constant US$ as forecast by the Bank
and converted to current DR. The price CIF Casablanca is indexed
(basis 1987) on the FOB price.
Salaries: indexed or. number of employees and local inflation.
Depreciation: Production assets 5.11, transmission assets 4.5,
distribution assets 7.22. Studies are expensed after five years.
Income tax: 452 of net income before tax minus Special Fund
allocation. The income tax credit carry over will be exhausted in
1989.
Other taxes: mostly VAT on sales (7X), patente, property taxes.
Other operating expenses: split into those indexed on yearly
investment (TFSE) and those indexed on gross fixed assets in service
and inflation, both on a 1986 basis.



- 108 -        ANNEX 14.4
Page 2 of 3
Other income: amortization of consumers' contributions. The
contributions existing on 12/31/86 are amortized over four years for tax
purposes. The future ones are amortized over fourteen years. Allocation
of net income to Special Fund: 4.5S of sales net of VAT.
Sources and aDplications of funds
Rescheduled interest: The three reachedulings have been considered as a
postponement of debt service payment. Accordingly, the rescheduled
interest has been accrued.
Contributions: Government NREP contributions correspond to the part (501)
of the NREP construction program which enters into ONE's assets.
Consumers' contributions: include ONE's mark-up on works performed by ONE
for customers.
Borrowing: the structure of ONE's borrowing is determined by the nature
of its investment program, which provides an upper limit to the amount of
(foreign) loans and suppliers' credits. The balance of borrowing is
ensured by the issuance of bonds in the local market.
Proposed Bank Loan: 7.762, 20 years including 5 years of grace
Production loans: 91, 15 years including 5 years of grace
Other loans: 91, 5 years, no grace
Bonds: 131, 15 years, no grace
Other sources: pension fund and Government bonds issued after PERL debt
consolidation. The PERL consolidation has been assumed to take place in
1987.
Balance Sheet
Gross fixed assets in service: unrevalued
Work in progress: transferred after completion according to ONE's
investment program.
Other non-current assets
(a) Government bonds: issued after PERL debt consolidation in 1987 and,
reimbursable over five years by equal installments starting in 1987.
(b) Other: studies, expensed after five years.



- 109 -
ANNEX 14.4
Page 3 of 3
Receivables
(a)   Energy (after the 1987 PERL settlement) - administrations: four
months of sales. Ragies and Offices: one mouth of sales. Private
consumers: 1.5 month of sales.
(b)   Works: indexed on inflation (basis 1986)
(c)   Other
VAT receivable: indexed on suppliers (oil, coal and others) for the year
customs duties receivable: indexed on investment (foreign) for the year.
Inventories
Oil and local coal: one month consumption
Imported coal: three months consumption
Other: indexed (basis 1986) on gross fixed assets in service and
inflation.
Consumers' contributions: they are amortized (see other income)
Other long-term liabilities: pension fund. Increases by 4% of salaries
(interest 92)
Suppliers (after 1987 PERL settlement):
oil and local coal: one month purchases
imported coal: four months purchases
other: indexed on yearly investment (1986 basis)
IBRD 1299-MOR & KFW: arrears on debt service of loans onlent to ONE by
the Government.  Assumed to be repaid in full in 1987 (PERL)
Other current liabilities
Line of credit: DR140 million from 1989
Interest payable: indexed on interest expense
Income tax payable: see income statement
Other: 102 yearly increase.

117 -            ~~~~ANNEX 1.5.6
- 117 -                 Page 1 of 3
MOROCCO
POWER DISTRIBUTON PROJECT
Rdgie of Casablana
Notes and assumptions on the financial statements
Each R4gie has its own accounting system.  The statements presented by
the Bank have been standardized and include several reclassifications. They
have been prepared in collaboration with the R6gies' financial departments.
The inflation indexes are the same as those for ONE (Annex 14-4).
Income statement
Sales: tarflf increases are assumed to take place on May 1. Sales are net of
the VAT ttx.
Developme-t surtax: a surcharge on normal tariffs, levied by some R6gies, to
help financo their investment. Generally indexed on sales (GWR). There is no
development sartax in Casablanca.
Other fees and charges: meter rental. Indexed on number of meters and
inflation (basis 1986).
Income on works in participation: 20Z on the amount of works in participation
(connection works paid for by consumers).
Other revenues: interest on current account (water): from '988, interest (122)
on average balance of the arrears from the Water Department existing at the
end of 1987. Maintenance work on connections: indexed on n;unber of
connections and inflation (basis 1986). Sundry revenues: rental of buildings
and equipment, penalties on contracts-indexed on number of cennections and
inflation (basis 1986).
Energy purchases: tariff increases (assumed to take place on May 1), are those
which have been determined from ONE's appraisal.  Purchase prices are net of
tax (VAT).
Investment program: for projections purposes, the investment program (as given
by the R6gies) has been split between salaries, materials and contractors
(TFSE). The salaries component has been indexed on the number of employees
and inflation. The percentage of materials has been kept constant and the
contractors item has been obtained by difference.
Materials:
a) investment: obtained from the breakdown of the investment program;
b) current: indexed (basis 1986) on gross fixed assets in operation and
inflation.



- 118 -                      ANNEX 15.6
Page 2 of 3
Salaries and wages: indexed on number of employees and inflation.
Taxes (indirect): no indirect taxes on investment after 1987. Current taxes
indexed on inflation (basis 1989).
Depreciation: the Regie does not depreciate its network, but only light
equipment (cars, etc.). Therefore, the network depreciation for tax purposes
has been added up to 1986. After 1986, the same constant 1986 percentage has
been applied.
Water Department Services: indexed on assets in operations (1986) and
inflation.
Contractors: obtained from the breakdown of the yearly investment program.
Income tax: as a 451 rate on (operating income before tax less interest
expense) less income on works in participation.
Other expenses: interest on ONE arrears: from 1988, interest (121) on average
balance of ONE arrears existing at the end of 1987.
Other: indexed on number of employees and inflation.
Sources and aOfications offunds
Borrowing: in addition to the Bank loan, it has been assumed that the Fonds
d'Equipement Communal (FEC) will provide the resources needed.
Proposed Bank loan: 7.76S, reimbursable over 15 years, grace period 5 years.
FEC loans: each yearly disbursement is considered as a separate loan (132,
constant annuity payment, reimbursable over 7 years, no grace period).
Consumers' contributions: generally, these contributions include the actual
cost of the works in participation (investment for new connections made by the
Regies and faid for by customers) plus a contribution to existing
infrastructure. The total customers' contributions for a given year have been
estimated by computing a average ratio over the past three years' customers'
contributions for works in participation and multiplying it by the works in
participation for the year.
Balance sheet
Accumulated depreciation: reconstituted up to 1986 from the R6gies' inception
on the basis of the depreciation of the network for tax purposes to which was
added the accumulated depreciation on light equipment.
Work in progress: the R6gies have no work in progress account and investment
is first transferred to inventories, from which it flows directly to gross
fixed assets in operation when commissioned. Therefore a work in progress



- 119 -                       ANNEX 15.6
Page 3 of 3
account has been created equal to 402 of the yearly investment (60S percent of
the yearly investment is transferred during the year).
Cash: in normal years, cash has been taken equal to one month of salaries plus
one month of materials (current).
Accounts receivable: Government (energy): arrears are eliminated in 1988 as a
consequence of the PERL settlement. Current billings are equal to four months
of sales (because of the 1984 circular).
Other consumers (energy): current billings are equal to one month of sales for
MV and two months for LV.
Other receivables: salary advances to employees and training center: indexed
on number of staff and inflation (basis 1986). End-of-year adjustment
accounts: indexed on inflation (basis 1986).
Current Account-Water Department: assumed to be repaid by equal installments
over five years up to 1992.
Suppliers: ONE: The PERL settlement is assu.sed to take place in 1987. It will
leave a balance of arrears towards ONE. This balance is assumed to be
eliminated over five years up to 1992. Current billings.are equal to 1.2
months of purchases.
Other suppliers: indexed (basis 1986) on the investment program of the year.
Consumers' deposits: computed from the cumulative number of additional meters.
Other current liabilities: unallocated payments from administrations and
private consumers have been eliminated from 1988 and 1989 respectively.
VAT payable on margin: one month of margin.
End-of-year adjustment accounts: indexed on inflation (basis 1986).

MOROCCO
POWER DISTRIBUTION PROJECT
RATE OF RETURN ANALYSIS
1.      The economic analysis of the project is set out in Attachment 1 of
this Annex and was carried out on the basis that the,project forms an integral
part of the investment program for ONE and the five participating Regies over
the period 1988-1994. The program is estimated to have an economic rate of
return of 12.4%. The main assumptions used to make the analysis are set out
here.
2.      Benefits  - The benefits include the incremental revenues for ONE and
the five R6gies for the period 1988-1994 plus benefits from rehabilitation
expenditures. The annual benefits were kept constant at the 1994 level from
1995 through 2021. The year 2021 marks the expected end of the useful life of
transmission and distribution facilities brought into service between 1988 and
1994. The revenue estimates were made in December 1987 prices by multiplying
the deflated tariff rates projected in the financial analyses to be necessary
to ensure an adequate level of self-financing for the power subsector (Annexes
14 and 15) by the projected incremental sales quantities (shown in the same
Annexes). The revenue estimates shown for ONE exclude revenues from bulk
sales to the five participating R6gies. The revenue estimates for the R6gies
include a charge of 20% of costs of connection of new customers since the
operating and maintenance costs include overhead costs which this charge is
intended to cover.
3.      The rehabilitation benefits include reductions in distribution losses,
estimated to reach 1.2S of total sales by ONE and the five R6gies by 1992; and
reduced operating and maintenance costs for ONE, estimated at a level which
would yield a 10 rate of return on the non-distribution system rehabilitation
investments included in the proposed project.
4.      Costs - The costs include: incremental tatel costs of ONE; incremental
operating and maintenance costs of ONE and the five R6gies; and investments
made by ONE and these Regies for the period 1988 through 1994.
5.      Incremental fuel costs were calculated using international prices for
fuel oil and coal ($104 per ton and $50 per ton respectively CIF at the power
stations). In order to'avoid a downward bias in the fuel cost estimates
caused by increased hydro electricity generation following 1987's
drought-influenced level, the incremental fuel costs were calculated on the
assumption of average hydroelectricity generation every year including 1988.
Fuel consumption by generating unit was projected using data on load duration
curves and unit heat rates supplied by ONE. The annual incremental fuel cost
level falls after 1994 as a result of increased utilization of the second 300
MW coal-fired generating unit at Jorf Lasfar which is projected to enter
service in 1994.



ANNEX 16
- 133-                             Page 2 of 3
6.       Incremental operating and maintenance coStS for ONE were assumed to
be 2S of incremental capital assets, Incremental operating and maintenance
costs for the five R6gies were calculated from the estimates given in the
financial projections (Annex 15) deflated to December 1987 prices.  The
procedure used va first to calculate the average operating and maintenance
cost per GWh of sales by each entity for each year and then to multiply this
average by the incremental sales quantity for the corresponding year compared
to the base year 1987. The reason for not using the same procedure for ONE is
that the incremental costs calculated in this manner would include not just
costs corresponding to new investments and sales, but also increased costs of
maintenance of previously constructed power stations incurred because of aging.
7.       The analysis includes only those investments which correspond to the
identified incremental benefits (Annexes 6 and 7 present ONE's investment
program). Investment expenditures made between 1988 and 1994 for thermal and
hydro units projected to come into service after 1994 were omitted. The
capital costs of connections and other capital expenditures financed by
customers were omitted. Another omission waS for rehabilitation investments
other than those included in the proposed Project, since their benefits could
not be estimated. Adjustments were made for the projected retirement of 135
Mg of construction turbine capacity and 60 MW of coal-fired capacity by
subtracting investment costs corresponding to the same capacities from
investments in new capacity, on the assumption that the corresponding part of
the nw capacity would be needed to serve existing demands rather than meet
new demands after 1987. It was necessary to include in the investment
estimates the expenditures made before 1988 on the Hassan I hydro project and
the La&youne diesel power station both of which will enter service before
1990.    Also included was a share of the costs of the dam and other civil
works for the Matmata project which are paid by the Government rather than ONE
(based on an estimate by NEDECO/C.I.D. in its "Feasibility Study of the
Matmata Project" January 1985). Subject to these adjustments, the investment
expenditures include those for. Kassan r, Matmata, the small Sidi Driss hydro
generating unit, 2X100 MW construction turbines and replacement units
projected to enter service in 2009 and 2010, 2x300 MW coal-fired units at Jorf
Lasfar, the La&youne diesel power station, all transmission and distribution
investments over the period 1988 through 1994 included in ONE's general
program of investments plus investments financed by the special fund, thermal
and hydro studies, and those rehabilitation investments included in the
proposed Project. For those generating units expected to continue in service
beyond 2025 a benefit was estimated by calculating the present value in 2021
of the stream of annuities for the period from 2021 until the end of their
useful lines, where the annuity for each unit was chosen so as to yield an
internal rate of return of 102 on the original investment.
8.       Sensitivity Tests - Several sensitivity tests yielded the following
results, in terms of the changes which would cause the economic rate of return
to decline from 12.41 to the opportunity cost of capital, estimated to be 10%:
Tariff rates                                        -101
Investment costs                                    +22X
Fuel costs                                          +332
2564L/28



ANNEX 16
Page 3 of 3
- 134 -
9.       The economic rate of return was also calculated using a shadow rate
of foreign exchange, estimated by Sank staff to be US$1 u DR 10.40 (compared
to the December 1987 rate of US$1 * DR 8.0). The result is a rate of 82.
10.      A further calculation of the economic rate of return was made where
benefits were amended to include the consumer's surplus on the incremental
sales. The consumer's surplus was estimated on the assumption of a constant
elasticity of demand equal to -0.3. The resulting calculations yield an
economic rate of return of 311.
